Read with `STATUS.md` (state), `CROSSCHECK.md` (the full task-#7 design + per-instruction

both Lean and Coq — see the git log and `PROOF.md`. The live frontier is now task #7.

## TL;DR of where we are

- **Everything builds green**: `cd coq && make -jN`; `cd lean && lake build`; `cd bare && make run` → `Hello\n`.
- **T1 (decode cross-check) is COMPLETE** — `coq/RvCross.v`, `decode_agrees`. Our

  `Rrel` + `WFstep` (the §5 alignment / data-domain side conditions, all true of `core`),

1	/-
2	  Faithful port of the hex0 grammar from `HEX0.md`, and its correspondence to
3	  the functional spec `decodeS` (`Hex0/Spec.lean`).
4	
5	  HEX0.md:
6	    GRAMMAR ::= <TOKEN>*
7	    TOKEN   ::= <BYTE> | <COMMENT> | <SPACING>
8	    BYTE    ::= <NIBBLE><NIBBLE>
9	    NIBBLE  ::= "0".."9" | "A".."F"
10	    COMMENT ::= ("#" | ";") (ALL_CHARS - "\n")* "\n"
11	    SPACING ::= " " | "_" | "\n"
12	    Each <BYTE> emits one output byte = high*16 + low.
13	
14	  Plan (this file):
15	    1. `Valid inp out` — the grammar as an inductive relation (the *valid*,
16	       error-free language), one constructor per production.
17	    2. `valid_ok` — every valid program decodes to exactly `(out, Ok)`.
18	    3. `decode_ok_valid` — the converse: if `decodeS` says `Ok`, the input was
19	       valid. Together: `decodeS .High inp = (out, Ok)  ↔  Valid inp out`.
20	    4. Error characterization + the divergences from HEX0.md's prose.
21	-/
22	import Hex0.Spec
23	
24	namespace Hex0
25	
26	/-! ## Small spec lemmas (local copies; depend only on `Spec`). -/
27	
28	/-- A hex digit is neither a comment nor a spacing char. -/
29	theorem nibble_not_comment {c v : Nat} (h : nibble c = some v) : isComment c = false := by
30	  simp only [nibble] at h
31	  by_cases hd : 48 ≤ c ∧ c ≤ 57
32	  · obtain ⟨h1, h2⟩ := hd; simp only [isComment, c_hash, c_semi, Bool.or_eq_false_iff,
33	      beq_eq_false_iff_ne]; omega
34	  · rw [if_neg hd] at h
35	    by_cases hl : 65 ≤ c ∧ c ≤ 70
36	    · obtain ⟨h1, h2⟩ := hl; simp only [isComment, c_hash, c_semi, Bool.or_eq_false_iff,
37	        beq_eq_false_iff_ne]; omega
38	    · rw [if_neg hl] at h; exact absurd h (by simp)
39	
40	theorem nibble_not_space {c v : Nat} (h : nibble c = some v) : isSpace c = false := by
41	  simp only [nibble] at h
42	  by_cases hd : 48 ≤ c ∧ c ≤ 57
43	  · obtain ⟨h1, h2⟩ := hd; simp only [isSpace, c_nl, c_sp, c_us, Bool.or_eq_false_iff,
44	      beq_eq_false_iff_ne]; omega
45	  · rw [if_neg hd] at h
46	    by_cases hl : 65 ≤ c ∧ c ≤ 70
47	    · obtain ⟨h1, h2⟩ := hl; simp only [isSpace, c_nl, c_sp, c_us, Bool.or_eq_false_iff,
48	        beq_eq_false_iff_ne]; omega
49	    · rw [if_neg hl] at h; exact absurd h (by simp)
50	
51	theorem nibble_not_lowstop {c v : Nat} (h : nibble c = some v) : isLowStop c = false := by
52	  simp only [isLowStop, nibble_not_space h, nibble_not_comment h, Bool.or_self]
53	
54	/-- A spacing char is not a comment char. -/
55	theorem space_not_comment {c : Nat} (h : isSpace c = true) : isComment c = false := by
56	  simp only [isSpace, c_nl, c_sp, c_us, beq_iff_eq, Bool.or_eq_true] at h
57	  simp only [isComment, c_hash, c_semi, Bool.or_eq_false_iff, beq_eq_false_iff_ne]; omega
58	
59	/-! ## `decodeS` token-decomposition lemmas (one per token class). -/
60	
61	theorem decodeS_spacing (c : Nat) (rest : List Nat)
62	    (hc : isComment c = false) (hs : isSpace c = true) :
63	    decodeS .High (c :: rest) = decodeS .High rest := by
64	  rw [decodeS]; simp [hc, hs]
65	
66	theorem decodeS_byte (chi clo : Nat) (rest : List Nat) (hi lo : Nat)
67	    (hc : isComment chi = false) (hs : isSpace chi = false) (hh : nibble chi = some hi)
68	    (hlc : isLowStop clo = false) (hl : nibble clo = some lo) :
69	    decodeS .High (chi :: clo :: rest) =
70	      ((hi * 16 + lo) :: (decodeS .High rest).1, (decodeS .High rest).2) := by
71	  rw [decodeS]; simp only [hc, hs, hh, Bool.false_eq_true, if_false]
72	  rw [decodeS]; simp [hlc, hl]
73	
74	theorem decodeS_comment (c : Nat) (rest : List Nat) (hc : isComment c = true) :
75	    decodeS .High (c :: rest) = decodeS .High (skipComment rest) := by
76	  rw [decodeS]; simp [hc]
77	
78	/-- `skipComment` over a newline-free body terminated by a newline yields the tail. -/
79	theorem skipComment_body (body rest : List Nat) (h : ∀ b ∈ body, b ≠ c_nl) :
80	    skipComment (body ++ c_nl :: rest) = rest := by
81	  induction body with
82	  | nil => show skipComment (c_nl :: rest) = rest; rfl
83	  | cons b bs ih =>
84	    have hb : b ≠ c_nl := h b Lis

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  03:41:53; tool 11ms

```
1	(** * hex0 functional specification (the refinement target)
2	
3	    This is the SHARED spec: the Lean file Hex0/Spec.lean mirrors it
4	    definition-for-definition. Bytes are modelled as [nat] (assumed < 256);
5	    the input is a [list nat].
6	
7	    The spec is a two-state machine (EXPECT_HIGH / EXPECT_LOW), written as a
8	    single well-founded recursion [decodeS] over an explicit state [St], so
9	    there is exactly one termination argument (decreasing on input length).
10	
11	    Reconciliation of sources:
12	      - HEX0.md gives the grammar + error names.
13	      - hex0.c (`unhex`) is the executable reference.
14	      - bare/core.s is the artifact the refinement proof concerns.
15	    In LOW position the five "stop" characters (\n ' ' '_' '#' ';') yield
16	    [Split]; any other non-hex character yields [Unknown]; EOF yields
17	    [Trailing]. Capacity (OutputShort) is NOT part of [decode] -- it is a
18	    property of the bounded machine, applied separately in [coreSpec]. *)
19	
20	From Coq Require Import List Arith Lia Bool.
21	From Equations Require Import Equations.
22	Import ListNotations.
23	Local Open Scope nat_scope.
24	Local Open Scope bool_scope.
25	
26	(* Character codes used by hex0. *)
27	Definition c_nl    := 10.   (* '\n' *)
28	Definition c_sp    := 32.   (* ' '  *)
29	Definition c_us    := 95.   (* '_'  *)
30	Definition c_hash  := 35.   (* '#'  *)
31	Definition c_semi  := 59.   (* ';'  *)
32	
33	Definition isSpace   (c:nat) : bool := (c =? c_nl) || (c =? c_sp) || (c =? c_us).
34	Definition isComment (c:nat) : bool := (c =? c_hash) || (c =? c_semi).
35	(* the characters that, seen where a low nibble is expected, give Split *)
36	Definition isLowStop (c:nat) : bool := isSpace c || isComment c.
37	
38	(* nibble value 0..15, or None if c is not an uppercase hex digit. *)
39	Definition nibble (c:nat) : option nat :=
40	  if (48 <=? c) && (c <=? 57) then Some (c - 48)        (* '0'..'9' *)
41	  else if (65 <=? c) && (c <=? 70) then Some (c - 55)   (* 'A'..'F' -> 10..15 *)
42	  else None.
43	
44	(* Terminal status of a decode (capacity-independent). *)
45	Inductive Status := Ok | Split | Trailing | Unknown.
46	
47	(* Skip a comment body: drop characters up to and including the first '\n'.
48	   (In core.s the '\n' is left for the main loop and skipped there as spacing;
49	   the net effect is the same -- continue at the character after the newline.) *)
50	Fixpoint skipComment (l:list nat) : list nat :=
51	  match l with
52	  | [] => []
53	  | c :: rest => if c =? c_nl then rest else skipComment rest
54	  end.
55	
56	Lemma skipComment_len : forall l, length (skipComment l) <= length l.
57	Proof.
58	  induction l as [|c rest IH]; simpl; [lia|].
59	  destruct (c =? c_nl); simpl; lia.
60	Qed.
61	
62	(* Decoder state. *)
63	Inductive St := High | Low (hi:nat).
64	
65	Equations? decodeS (s:St) (l:list nat) : (list nat * Status) by wf (length l) lt :=
66	  decodeS High [] := ([], Ok);
67	  decodeS (Low _) [] := ([], Trailing);
68	  decodeS High (c :: rest) :=
69	    if isComment c then decodeS High (skipComment rest)
70	    else if isSpace c then decodeS High rest
71	    else match nibble c with
72	         | None => ([], Unknown)
73	         | Some hi => decodeS (Low hi) rest
74	         end;
75	  decodeS (Low hi) (c :: rest) :=
76	    if isLowStop c then ([], Split)
77	    else match nibble c with
78	         | None => ([], Unknown)
79	         | Some lo => let '(out, st) := decodeS High rest in
80	                      (hi * 16 + lo :: out, st)
81	         end.
82	Proof.
83	  all: simpl in *; try lia.
84	  all: match goal with
85	       | [ |- context[length (skipComment ?l)] ] =>
86	           pose proof (skipComment_len l); lia
87	       end.
88	Qed.
89	
90	Definition decode (l:list nat) : (list nat * Status) := decodeS High l.
91	
92	(* Numeric status codes, matching the Error enum in hex0.c / core.s. *)
93	Definition statusCode (s:Status) : nat :=
94	  match s with Ok => 0 | Split => 3 | Trailing => 4 |
… [truncated 564 chars]
```

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  03:41:53; model 153ms

```json
{"file_path": "/var/data/bootstrap/lean/Hex0/Spec.lean"}

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  03:41:53; tool 7ms

```
1	/-
2	  hex0 functional specification (the refinement target).
3	
4	  This MIRRORS coq/Spec.v definition-for-definition. Bytes are modelled as
5	  `Nat` (assumed < 256); the input is a `List Nat`.
6	
7	  The spec is a two-state machine (EXPECT_HIGH / EXPECT_LOW), written as a
8	  single well-founded recursion `decodeS` over an explicit state `St`, so there
9	  is exactly one termination argument (decreasing on input length).
10	
11	  In LOW position the five "stop" characters (\n ' ' '_' '#' ';') yield `Split`;
12	  any other non-hex character yields `Unknown`; EOF yields `Trailing`. Capacity
13	  (OutputShort) is NOT part of `decode` -- it is applied separately in `coreSpec`.
14	-/
15	
16	namespace Hex0
17	
18	/-- Character codes used by hex0. -/
19	def c_nl   : Nat := 10   -- '\n'
20	def c_sp   : Nat := 32   -- ' '
21	def c_us   : Nat := 95   -- '_'
22	def c_hash : Nat := 35   -- '#'
23	def c_semi : Nat := 59   -- ';'
24	
25	def isSpace   (c : Nat) : Bool := c == c_nl || c == c_sp || c == c_us
26	def isComment (c : Nat) : Bool := c == c_hash || c == c_semi
27	/-- characters that, where a low nibble is expected, give `Split`. -/
28	def isLowStop (c : Nat) : Bool := isSpace c || isComment c
29	
30	/-- nibble value 0..15, or `none` if `c` is not an uppercase hex digit. -/
31	def nibble (c : Nat) : Option Nat :=
32	  if 48 ≤ c ∧ c ≤ 57 then some (c - 48)        -- '0'..'9'
33	  else if 65 ≤ c ∧ c ≤ 70 then some (c - 55)   -- 'A'..'F' -> 10..15
34	  else none
35	
36	/-- Terminal status of a decode (capacity-independent). -/
37	inductive Status where
38	  | Ok | Split | Trailing | Unknown
39	deriving DecidableEq, Repr
40	
41	/-- Drop characters up to and including the first '\n'. -/
42	def skipComment : List Nat → List Nat
43	  | [] => []
44	  | c :: rest => if c == c_nl then rest else skipComment rest
45	
46	theorem skipComment_len : ∀ l, (skipComment l).length ≤ l.length
47	  | [] => Nat.le_refl 0
48	  | c :: rest => by
49	      simp only [skipComment]
50	      split
51	      · exact Nat.le_succ_of_le (Nat.le_refl _)
52	      · exact Nat.le_succ_of_le (skipComment_len rest)
53	
54	/-- Decoder state. -/
55	inductive St where
56	  | High | Low (hi : Nat)
57	
58	def decodeS : St → List Nat → (List Nat × Status)
59	  | .High, [] => ([], .Ok)
60	  | .Low _, [] => ([], .Trailing)
61	  | .High, c :: rest =>
62	      if isComment c then decodeS .High (skipComment rest)
63	      else if isSpace c then decodeS .High rest
64	      else match nibble c with
65	           | none => ([], .Unknown)
66	           | some hi => decodeS (.Low hi) rest
67	  | .Low hi, c :: rest =>
68	      if isLowStop c then ([], .Split)
69	      else match nibble c with
70	           | none => ([], .Unknown)
71	           | some lo =>
72	               let (out, st) := decodeS .High rest
73	               ((hi * 16 + lo) :: out, st)
74	  termination_by _ l => l.length
75	  decreasing_by
76	    all_goals simp_wf
77	    · have h := skipComment_len rest; omega
78	    all_goals omega
79	
80	def decode (l : List Nat) : List Nat × Status := decodeS .High l
81	
82	/-- Numeric status codes, matching the Error enum in hex0.c / core.s. -/
83	def statusCode : Status → Nat
84	  | .Ok => 0 | .Split => 3 | .Trailing => 4 | .Unknown => 5
85	
86	/-- Behaviour of the bounded machine `core` with output capacity `cap`:
87	    if the decode would emit more than `cap` bytes, the machine stops with
88	    OutputShort (code 2) having written exactly the first `cap` bytes.
89	    Returns (status, output, out_len). -/
90	def coreSpec (input : List Nat) (cap : Nat) : Nat × List Nat × Nat :=
91	  let (bs, st) := decode input
92	  if cap < bs.length then (2, bs.take cap, cap)
93	  else (statusCode st, bs, bs.length)
94	
95	end Hex0
96	
```

(** * RvCross.v -- cross-validation of our RV64I model against riscv-coq.

    Task #7 (see CROSSCHECK.md): remove "our hand-rolled RV64I model is faithful
    to real RISC-V" from the TCB by proving our [Rv64i.decode]/[Rv64i.step] agree
    with the authoritative riscv-coq semantics (coq-riscv.0.0.5, the bedrock2 /
    compiler model, generated from the official Haskell riscv-semantics).

    T1 ([decode_agrees]): whenever our decoder returns one of the 12 modelled
    instructions, riscv-coq's [Decode.decode RV64I] returns the corresponding
    instruction with identical operands -- for every 32-bit word.

    T2 ([step_agrees], forward simulation): one of our [step]s corresponds to one
    riscv-coq instruction cycle, preserving a state-bridge relation. *)

From Coq Require Import ZArith List Bool Lia.
Import ListNotations.
Require Import Hex0Coq.Rv64i.
Require Import riscv.Spec.Decode.
Require Import riscv.Utility.Utility.
Require Import coqutil.Z.BitOps.
Require Import coqutil.Z.prove_Zeq_bitwise.
Local Open Scope Z_scope.

(* ------------------------------------------------------------------ *)
(* Bridging lemmas: our field/sext primitives vs riscv-coq's          *)
===RvCrossStep head===
(** * RvCrossStep.v -- foundations for the execute/step cross-check (task #7, T2).

    Forward-simulation of our [Rv64i.step] against riscv-coq's [Run.run1 RV64I]
    over the Minimal [OState] machine (coq-riscv.0.0.5). This file establishes the
    two foundational, instruction-independent pieces of that simulation, both
    [Admitted]-free:

    - the WORD/Z ARITHMETIC BRIDGE: every riscv-coq [word 64] operation that
      [ExecuteI] uses (add / or / unsigned-< / signed-<) computes our corresponding
      [Z]-mod-2^64 operation (wadd / wor / ultb / sltb) under [word.unsigned];
    - the FETCH BRIDGE [fetch_combine]: one [run1] instruction fetch
      (combine of the 4 little-endian bytes that [load_bytes 4] reads) equals the
      32-bit word our [fetch32] reads, given the riscv memory map agrees with our
      byte memory on the 4 fetch addresses.

    Also recorded: the state-bridge relation [Rrel] / well-formedness [WFrel]
    (CROSSCHECK.md §3) that [step_agrees] will use. Remaining for T2: the [run1]
    monad reduction + the 12 per-instruction [exec_*] lemmas + [step_agrees] +
    the transport corollary [core_refines_riscv]. *)

===how decodeS unfolds: simp lemma names===

36	Lemma nibble_range : forall c v, nibble c = Some v -> 48 <= c <= 57 \/ 65 <= c <= 70.
37	Proof.
38	  intros c v. unfold nibble.
39	  destruct (Nat.leb_spec 48 c) as [H1|H1]; simpl;
40	  destruct (Nat.leb_spec c 57) as [H2|H2]; simpl;
41	  destruct (Nat.leb_spec 65 c) as [H3|H3]; simpl;
42	  destruct (Nat.leb_spec c 70) as [H4|H4]; simpl;
43	  intro H; try discriminate; lia.
44	Qed.
45	
46	(** A hex digit is neither a comment nor a spacing char. *)
47	Lemma nibble_not_comment : forall c v, nibble c = Some v -> isComment c = false.

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  03:51:56; model 17.4s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Done. The port is complete and verified.

## What I did

Ported `lean/Hex0/Grammar.lean` to a new file **`coq/Grammar.v`** (added to `coq/_CoqProject`). The Coq `Spec.v` already mirrored `Spec.lean`'s functional spec (`nibble`, `isComment`, `isSpace`, `isLowStop`, `skipComment`, `Status`, `decodeS`), so only the grammar layer was missing.

It's a **theorem-for-theorem** port — all 28 Lean declarations have Coq twins (plus one extra helper, `nibble_range`, that Lean got for free from `omega`):

- **`Valid : list nat → list nat → Prop`** — the error-free grammar as an inductive relation, one constructor per BNF production (nil / byte / spacing / commentNl / commentEof).
- **`valid_ok`** — every valid program decodes to `(out, Ok)`.
- **`Parse : list nat → list nat → Status → Prop`** — the full grammar with the HEX0.md error taxonomy (errUnknownHigh / errTrailing / errSplit / errUnknownLow).
- **`parse_sound`** — whatever the grammar derives, `decodeS` computes (output + status).
- **`parse_complete` / `parse_total`** — every input is derivable (strong induction on length).
- **`parse_det`** — the grammar is deterministic.
- **`valid_or_err` / `not_valid_and_err`** — valid/erroneous is a total, disjoint partition.
- Supporting `decodeS_*` token-decomposition and error lemmas, `skipComment_body/_no_nl`, `newline_split`, and the two sanity examples.

## Verification

- `cd coq && make -j4` → **green** (`COQC Grammar.v`, full dev builds).
- `grep Admitted/admit/Axiom/sorry coq/Grammar.v` → **NONE**.
- `Print Assumptions` on `valid_ok`, `parse_sound`, `parse_complete`, `parse_det` → only **`functional_extensionality_dep`** — the same axiom footprint as the rest of the Coq dev (it comes from the `Equations`-based well-founded `decodeS`, not from anything in the port). No `Classical`.

A few Coq-specific adaptations were needed where Lean's `simp`/`omega` don't transfer directly: `nibble_range` is proved by an `eqn`-based case split feeding `lia`, and the `skipComment` lemmas use `cbn [skipComment app]` instead of `simpl` to avoid prematurely unfolding the `c_nl` literal.

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

You're right to be skeptical, and to be precise: it *wasn't* correct from the very first compile. Let me be honest about what actually happened and why it went as smoothly as it did.

**It took two fixes before it compiled** (you can see them in the session):
1. `nibble_range` — my first proof via `Nat.leb_spec` failed with `lia: Cannot find witness`.
2. `skipComment_body` — `rewrite Nat.eqb_refl` failed because `simpl` had already over-reduced the `c_nl` literal; I had to switch to `cbn [skipComment app]`.

So the *proof scripts* needed iteration. What *was* right on the first try was the **definitions and theorem statements** — and that part isn't as surprising as it looks, for three concrete reasons:

1. **I didn't implement the function.** The function under all of this — `decodeS` — already existed in `coq/Spec.v` and has been battle-tested by the whole refinement proof (`Refine.v`). I only added the grammar *relations* (`Valid`, `Parse`, both inductive `Prop`s) on top of it. There was no new executable code to get wrong.

2. **The proof was already done once, in Lean.** This is a port. The Lean `Grammar.lean` is a complete, checked proof that these exact statements hold. I was transcribing a known-true roadmap, not discovering whether it's true.

3. **The hard spec-side lemmas pre-existed in Coq.** `decodeS_spacing`, `decodeS_byte`, `decodeS_comment`, the four error lemmas — `Refine.v` already had these with essentially identical statements and proof scripts (`simp decodeS. rewrite ...`). I reused those, so the load-bearing parts were proven Coq, not freshly invented.

That said — the legitimate worry behind your comment is *vacuity*: did it pass because it's genuinely faithful, or because the statements are trivially/vacuously true (or mismatched against a different object)? Let me actually check that rather than assert it.

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  04:36:36; model 32.6s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Now I can give you a straight answer. Here's the actual timeline:

| Commit | What landed |
|---|---|
| **1** `d92bcd7` | `HEX0.md` (prose grammar) + `hex0.c` (**177-line executable C reference**) |
| **2** `eb1210b` | `bare/core.s` (the 118-line RISC-V assembly) — *never modified again* |
| **3** `93cc666` | `coq/Spec.v` + `Spec.lean` — the **formal** `decodeS` spec |

That ordering explains both the benign part and the part you should stay suspicious of.

**Why the assembly plausibly *was* right first-commit (benign):**
- It's `hex0` — a deliberately trivial, very well-known bootstrap program (stage0 lineage). Its whole job is "read hex pairs → bytes, skip spaces/comments." 118 lines, mostly straight-line.
- It wasn't written against nothing: a **runnable C reference (`hex0.c`) was committed first**. `core.s` is a transcription of already-existing, testable code into assembly — exactly the kind of thing a careful author gets right on the first *commit*.
- Crucially: we cannot see pre-first-commit local iteration. "No iterations in git" ≠ "no debugging ever." The author may well have run it against `input.hex` until it worked, then committed the working version.

**Where your suspicion is actually well-aimed (the non-benign part):**
- The **formal spec `decodeS` was written *after* the program** (commit 3 after commit 2). So the refinement proof establishes `core.s ≡ decodeS`, but the proof *by itself* cannot rule out that `decodeS` was reverse-engineered to match what `core.s` already did. That's textbook spec-retrofitting risk.
- The mitigations are real but not airtight: there are three anchors (`HEX0.md` prose, `hex0.c` C reference, and validation against the *actual deployed bytes*), and the two earliest predate the program. But `hex0.c` and `core.s` were presumably written by the same author, so "assembly agrees with the C reference" is **not a fully independent check** — a shared misconception about what hex0 *should* do would be invisible to the entire proof stack.

So the precise thing the proof buys you is **internal consistency**: the deployed bytes faithfully refine a spec that agrees with the C reference and the prose grammar. What it does *not* buy you — and what first-try program correctness can lull you into overrating — is that "hex0 as this author understood it" equals "hex0 as the bootstrap ecosystem expects it." That last gap is a social/external-correctness question that lives outside the formal TCB, and no amount of Coq closes it.

Want me to check `TCB.md` to see whether the project already states this boundary explicitly, or diff `core.s` against `hex0.c` to see how mechanical the transcription actually was?

 ```
 
 Each `<BYTE>` corresponds to one output byte, treating the first `<NIBBLE>` as the high nibble, and the second `<NIBBLE>` as the low nibble.
 
+A `<COMMENT>` runs from `#`/`;` up to **and including** the next `"\n"`, or to **end of input** if no `"\n"` follows (an unterminated trailing comment is accepted). Comments and spacing produce no output.
+
+Define the **stop characters** as the characters that begin a `<SPACING>` or `<COMMENT>` token: `" "`, `"_"`, `"\n"`, `"#"`, `";"`.
+
 ## Errors:
 
-- `<NIBBLE>` followed by non-matching char: `ErrUnknownChar`
-- `<NIBBLE>` followed by non-`<NIBBLE>`: `ErrSplitNibble`
 - `<NIBBLE>` followed by `EOF`: `ErrTrailingNibble`

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  04:40:14; model 39.8s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

That diff is the whole story, and it confirms your point precisely. The grammar wasn't an independent oracle that the implementation was checked against — where they disagreed, **the grammar was edited to match the implementation** ("in favor of impl"). Two concrete divergences:

1. **Comment termination.** Prose grammar required `COMMENT ::= (#|;) (¬\n)* "\n"` — a comment *must* end in a newline. So an unterminated trailing comment (`# foo<EOF>`) would have been an error. The implementation accepts it. Grammar amended to `("\n" | EOF)`.

2. **The error taxonomy was genuinely self-contradictory.** The original two rules were:
   - `<NIBBLE>` followed by non-matching char → `ErrUnknownChar`
   - `<NIBBLE>` followed by non-`<NIBBLE>` → `ErrSplitNibble`
   
   A non-matching char *is* a non-nibble, so both rules fire on the same input and give different verdicts. Underspecified, period. The implementation draws the line at "stop character" (begins another token → `Split`) vs. "other garbage" (→ `Unknown`), and the grammar was rewritten to that.

So the circularity I flagged earlier isn't hypothetical — it's documented in a commit message. For those two points, the formal grammar (and my Coq port of it, which carries the `commentEof` constructor and the `errSplit`/`errUnknownLow` split) is **not** independent evidence. "core.s matches the grammar" is partly true by construction there.

But it's worth being precise about what still has content, because it's not nothing:

- **Totality + disjointness is exactly what *forced* the disambiguation.** You cannot prove `parse_det` (unique `(out,st)` per input) about a relation whose rules contradict each other — the overlapping Unknown-vs-Split rules literally can't coexist in a determinism proof. So proving disjointness is real mathematical content, and it's the thing that *surfaced* the underspecification rather than papering over it. That's the proof doing useful work, just not the work of validating the implementation's choices.
- **Only two edge cases were resolved-toward-impl.** The happy path (BYTE, SPACING, the high/low nibble machinery) was never in dispute; the refinement there is genuine.

The honest bottom line: for trailing-comment-at-EOF and the nibble-error subclassification, the *implementation* is the authority and the grammar is descriptive, not prescriptive. The stack proves grammar ≡ `decodeS` ≡ `core.s` are mutually consistent — which is what you want *if* you've decided the implementation defines correct hex0. It does not independently certify that those two judgment calls are the "right" hex0 semantics; that was the author's call, now baked consistently through Lean, the spec, and (as of my commit) Coq.

One side note relevant to my port: the Lean grammar commit lists axioms `propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound`. The Coq `Grammar.v` I committed is cleaner on that axis — only `functional_extensionality_dep`, no `Classical.choice` — but that's a proof-hygiene difference, not an independence difference. It inherits the same two impl-aligned decisions.

28	/-- A hex digit is neither a comment nor a spacing char. -/
29	theorem nibble_not_comment {c v : Nat} (h : nibble c = some v) : isComment c = false := by
30	  simp only [nibble] at h
31	  by_cases hd : 48 ≤ c ∧ c ≤ 57
32	  · obtain ⟨h1, h2⟩ := hd; simp only [isComment, c_hash, c_semi, Bool.or_eq_false_iff,
33	      beq_eq_false_iff_ne]; omega
34	  · rw [if_neg hd] at h
35	    by_cases hl : 65 ≤ c ∧ c ≤ 70

37	        beq_eq_false_iff_ne]; omega

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  04:45:58; model 10.3s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Done. Committed as `94d44f1`.

## Summary

`Classical.choice` is now gone from `Grammar.lean`. 

**Root cause** (the exact gotcha in your `lean-omega-classical-choice` memory): all the grammar theorems funneled through three character-class helpers — `nibble_not_comment`, `nibble_not_space`, `space_not_comment` — and each ended with `omega` on a **conjunction** goal like `c ≠ 35 ∧ c ≠ 59`. `omega` on a conjunction/iff goal reaches for `Classical.choice`.

**Fix:** split the goal into single `≠` leaves before `omega` (`refine ⟨?_, ?_⟩ <;> omega`, and `⟨⟨?_, ?_⟩, ?_⟩` for the 3-way `isSpace` case). `nibble_not_lowstop` and the `decodeS_{trailing,split,unknown_low}` error lemmas depended on those, so they cleaned up for free.

**Verified** with `#print axioms`:

| theorem | before | after |
|---|---|---|
| `valid_ok`, `parse_sound`, `parse_complete`, `parse_total`, `parse_det`, `valid_or_err`, `not_valid_and_err` | `propext, Classical.choice, Quot.sound` | `propext, Quot.sound` |
| `valid_to_parse` | (none) | (none) |

`propext` + `Quot.sound` are the standard non-classical Lean core axioms (unavoidable — they come from `decodeS`'s well-founded recursion and `List`/`Nat`), so this is the clean floor. Full `lake build` is green; the only linter notes are pre-existing ones in `Refine.lean`, untouched by this change.

This brings the Lean grammar's footprint in line with the `coq/Grammar.v` I committed earlier (`functional_extensionality_dep` only, no Classical).

The deprecation ones were genuine lint and are now gone — the Coq build emits **zero** deprecation warnings.

The `abstract-large-number` notes are **not a code smell**. They fire on any `nat` literal ≥ 5000 (the fuel bound `100000`, masks like `65536`/`16777216`) and just announce that Coq parsed the literal in binary via `Nat.of_num_uint` instead of unary `S (S …)` — which is the desired, stack-safe behavior. There's no source-level fix: naming a constant `Definition fuelBound : nat := 100000` just moves the literal, it still warns at the definition site.

The only way to silence them is blanket suppression — add to `coq/_CoqProject`:
```
-arg "-w -abstract-large-number"
```
I **didn't** do this, because unlike the deprecation it's hiding an informational message rather than fixing a problem, and it would also mask genuinely-accidental huge literals in the future. If you'd rather have a fully silent `make`, say the word and I'll add the flag; otherwise I'd recommend leaving these as-is.

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  04:54:28; model 33.1s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

The Claude "total" is misleading — it sums `cache_read` across every message (the cached context is re-read each turn, billed at ~0.1×), inflating to a meaningless 1.45 B. The honest metric is a cache-aware **cost breakdown**. Let me fix the presentation: separate the token components and add an estimated USD cost at standard Opus rates for Claude (and tokens-only for Codex, whose model pricing isn't public).

# Agent sessions for `/var/data/bootstrap`

Collected **9 Claude Code** session(s) and **5 Codex** session(s) whose working directory is this project.

Per-session transcripts, summaries, and token costs live under `claude/` and `codex/`. Each file has a header (model, turns, token cost), a summary (first request + final response), and the full transcript (long tool outputs truncated).

## Aggregate token cost

**Claude Code** (summed from per-message `usage`):

| Output | Fresh input | Cache write | Cache read | Est. cost (Opus rates) |
|--:|--:|--:|--:|--:|
| 2,986,831 | 171,925 | 5,999,614 | 701,639,828 | **$1,391.54** |

**Codex** (cumulative `total_token_usage` from each session's final `token_count`):

| Output | Total tokens |
|--:|--:|
| 39,258 | 5,473,155 |

> Notes: cache-read tokens are re-counted every turn (billed ~0.1×), so they dominate raw
> volume but little of the cost — hence the cache-aware USD estimate instead of a summed
> token 'total' for Claude. The Opus dollar figure uses standard public rates ($15/$75 per
> Mtok in/out, $18.75/$1.50 cache write/read) and is an **estimate**. Codex models
> (gpt-5.5, deepseek-v4-pro) have no public pricing, so only token counts are shown.

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  04:57:57; model 11.5s

Done. I collected every Claude Code and Codex session whose working directory is `/var/data/bootstrap` into `sessions/`, and copied the generator script in as requested.

## `sessions/` layout

```
sessions/
├── README.md              ← index + aggregate token cost + per-session tables
├── gen_sessions.py        ← the collector (re-runnable; rebuilds everything)
├── claude/01..09-*.md     ← 9 Claude Code sessions
└── codex/01..05-*.md      ← 5 Codex sessions
```

Each per-session file has a **header** (model, turns, tool calls, source path), a **token-cost** block, a **summary** (first request + final response), and the **full transcript** (assistant/user turns, thinking/reasoning, tool calls; long tool outputs truncated to keep files readable).

## Token cost

| Agent | Sessions | Output tokens | Cost / Total |
|---|--:|--:|--:|
| Claude Code | 9 | 2,989,354 | **≈ $1,393** (est., Opus rates) |
| Codex | 5 | 39,258 | 5,473,155 tok (no public pricing) |

## Two accounting subtleties I had to handle (so the numbers are honest)
- **Claude split-line dedup:** one assistant API response is logged as several jsonl lines (one per content block), each repeating the *same* `usage`. Naïvely summing tripled the output count (8.1M → correct 2.99M). I now count `usage` once per `requestId` and group the blocks into one turn.
- **Cache reads ≠ cost:** Claude re-counts the cached context every turn (701M cache-read tokens total), billed at ~0.1×. So I report a cache-aware **USD estimate** at standard Opus rates rather than a misleading summed "total." Codex's `total_token_usage` is already cumulative, taken from each session's final `token_count`.

Note: these live under the repo but I did **not** commit them (they're agent logs, not project source). If you want them ignored, I can add `sessions/` to `.gitignore`; if you want them committed, say so. Re-running `python3 sessions/gen_sessions.py` regenerates the whole tree.

# Agent sessions for `/var/data/bootstrap`

## Aggregate cost

| Agent | Sessions | Output tokens | Cost (USD) |
|---|--:|--:|--:|
| Claude Code | 9 | 3,004,357 | **$466.12** |
| Codex | 5 | 39,258 | **$4.31** |
| **All** | **14** | **3,043,615** | **$470.43** |

> **Pricing source:** openrouter.ai/api/v1/models (live). Cost is computed per token from each model's OpenRouter rates (prompt / completion / cache-read / cache-write), so cache-read tokens — re-counted every Claude turn — are billed at their reduced rate rather than inflating the headline. Model rate matches:
>
> - claude-opus-4-8 → `anthropic/claude-opus-4.8`
> - deepseek/deepseek-v4-pro → `deepseek/deepseek-v4-pro`

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  05:02:05; model 10.6s

The script now fetches live pricing from OpenRouter and prices every session — including Codex, which previously had no cost.

## What changed in `sessions/gen_sessions.py`

- **`load_pricing()`** — fetches `https://openrouter.ai/api/v1/models` (stdlib `urllib`, no API key needed) and caches the response to `sessions/openrouter_models.json`, so reruns work offline (falls back to the cache, then to "n/a" if neither is available).
- **`match_pricing()`** — maps each recorded model name to an OpenRouter id: exact match first, then a canonical fuzzy match (strips provider prefix and non-alphanumerics, so `claude-opus-4-8` → `anthropic/claude-opus-4.8`, while correctly *not* matching the pricier `-fast` variant).
- **`session_cost()`** — computes USD per-token from the matched rates (`prompt` / `completion` / `input_cache_read` / `input_cache_write`), correctly billing Claude's huge cache-read volume at its reduced rate, and splitting Codex's cached-vs-fresh input.

## Result

| Agent | Sessions | Output tok | Cost |
|---|--:|--:|--:|
| Claude Code | 9 | 3,004,357 | **$466.12** |
| Codex | 5 | 39,258 | **$4.31** |
| **All 14** | | **3,043,615** | **$470.43** |

All three models matched live rates:
- `claude-opus-4-8` → `anthropic/claude-opus-4.8` ($5/$25 per Mtok in/out, $0.50 cache-read)
- `openai/gpt-5.5` → `openai/gpt-5.5`
- `deepseek/deepseek-v4-pro` → `deepseek/deepseek-v4-pro`

The Claude figure dropped from the earlier $1,392 estimate because OpenRouter lists `claude-opus-4.8` at $5/$25 rather than the $15/$75 I'd hardcoded. Each per-session file's header now shows the matched OpenRouter id and the exact rates used. The script in `sessions/` is the final version; rerun `python3 sessions/gen_sessions.py` to refresh with current pricing.

### 👤 **User**  ·  05:02:51; waited 45.6s

does it mean that anthropic is under-pricing their model, since I get claude for $100/mo?

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  05:03:31; model 53.4s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Not really — and the number itself is misleading in a way that's worth unpacking. Three separate things are going on.

**1. The $466 is *list API value*, not Anthropic's cost — and it's ~75% cache reads.**
Decomposing that Claude figure at OpenRouter's `claude-opus-4.8` rates:

| Component | Tokens | Rate (/Mtok) | Cost |
|---|--:|--:|--:|
| cache **read** | ~702 M | $0.50 | **~$351** |
| output | ~3.0 M | $25 | ~$75 |
| cache **write** | ~6 M | $6.25 | ~$38 |
| fresh input | ~0.17 M | $5 | ~$1 |

About **$350 of the $466 is cache reads** — and those are the single cheapest tokens to serve (it's reused KV-cache, not recomputed attention over 700M tokens). List price has margin baked in on top of that. So Anthropic's actual marginal cost to serve these sessions is *far* below $466 — the headline overstates their cost a lot.

**2. It's a different product, priced on population averages.**
The $100/mo is a subscription; the $466 is metered pay-as-you-go. Subscriptions are priced so the plan is profitable across *all* subscribers, not per power user. Most people on a $100 plan use a fraction of the cap — they subsidize whales. You (multi-hour agentic proof sessions) are clearly a whale. A gym doesn't lose money because one member squats every day.

**3. Rate limits cap how much you can actually extract.**
That $466 was ~2 days of intense work. You can't run that continuously on the subscription — Max plans have 5-hour and weekly limits precisely so a single account can't pull unbounded API-equivalent value. The cap is the guardrail that makes the flat fee viable.

So the honest read: for a heavy user, the sub can deliver more *list-price value* than the monthly fee — that's real and intentional. But "under-pricing" implies a mistake or a loss, and that doesn't follow, because (a) list price ≫ their serving cost, especially when cache reads dominate, (b) light users subsidize heavy ones, and (c) rate limits bound the downside.

The one place your instinct is right: frontier-AI subscriptions *are* currently priced aggressively (the whole industry is in a land-grab, burning capital for growth/lock-in), so heavy users probably do come out ahead versus metered API. That's a deliberate growth strategy, not an accident.

Caveat: these are OpenRouter's listed rates for these model ids (with their markup), and I'm not certain of the current exact Max-plan limits — so treat the dollar figures as directional, not Anthropic's books.

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  05:10:43; model 23.1s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Resolved — it was two separate things, and digging in pinned both down precisely.

## The token counts (1.14M / 4.34M) are correct, just counter-intuitive
Codex's `total_token_usage` is **cumulative across every model call** in the session, and each call re-sends the whole growing context. So the gpt-5.5 session's 4.34M is ~32 calls × ~130k context — and **92% of it (3.98M) is cached re-sent input**, not new content. The counts matching OpenRouter's dashboard (1.14M / 4.34M) confirms my parsing is right; the number just *looks* huge because re-sent context is counted every turn.

## gpt-5.5 price — that was my bug, now fixed
The token structure gave it away: `total_tokens = input_tokens + output_tokens` **exactly**, and `reasoning_output_tokens` is *not* added in — so reasoning is a **subset** of `output_tokens`. My `session_cost` was adding it on top, double-counting reasoning. After the fix:
- gpt-5.5 → **$4.0976 ≈ $4.10**, and the back-solved cache-read rate is $0.5006/Mtok vs OpenRouter's listed $0.50 — exact to the cent. ✓

## deepseek ($0.06 vs your $0.36) — not a code bug; the rollout can't reproduce it
Back-solving, OpenRouter's $0.36 implies an **effective cache-read rate of ~$0.296/Mtok**, ~80× the listed $0.003625/Mtok. The reason: the rollout only stores Codex's **optimistic** `cached_input_tokens` (what it *expected* to hit cache), but billing only discounts tokens that *actually* hit (cache entries expire on a TTL). The math says ~⅓ of the "cached" tokens truly hit at the cheap rate and ~⅔ were billed near the full prompt rate. OpenAI's caching reconciled perfectly; DeepSeek's deep discount + TTL expiry didn't. The rollout has no per-generation cost field, so I can't reproduce $0.36 exactly — I've documented Codex costs as a **lower bound** in the README, while Claude (whose cache reads are reported *as billed*) stays exact.

Net: token counts right, gpt-5.5 now matches OpenRouter to the cent, deepseek is a flagged lower bound. (The Claude/total figures drift by a few thousand tokens between runs because session 9 is *this* live conversation, still being appended.) Script in `sessions/gen_sessions.py` updated.

Here's the honest result of scanning all 14 transcripts + the README:

## No credentials — clean
No API keys, tokens, passwords, private keys, `Authorization`/`x-api-key` headers, or SSH/AWS/GCP creds. The scary-looking regex hits were false positives: `sk-notification` is `<task-notification>`, and every `token` match is the hex0 grammar's `TOKEN ::=` BNF. The OpenRouter cache file is just public model pricing. The IPs `2.2.2.1/2.2.2.2` are the QEMU dummy test addresses from the bare-metal RISC-V setup.

## But there *is* personal/environment data
| What | Where | Severity |
|---|---|---|
| **Real name + email** — `<redacted-name> <<redacted-email>>` | `claude/09-…md` (one `git log` author line; email appears ~2×) | PII |
| **OS username `null`** via `/home/<user>/...` paths | all 14 files, ~268 occurrences | low — identity/host fingerprint |
| **Full `$PATH` dump** (opam, cargo, cuda, gradle, dotnet, depot_tools, opencode, claude plugins) | `claude/05-…md:694` | low — reveals installed toolchain/home layout |

None of it is a secret, but the name + email + username would identify you, and the `$PATH`/home paths fingerprint the machine. That matters only if these files leave your box — and right now they're **untracked**, so they won't be committed unless you add them.

## Options
1. **Leave as-is** — fine if they stay local.
2. **Scrub** — I can redact `<redacted-email>` → `<redacted-email>`, `<redacted-name>` → `<redacted-name>`, and `/home/<user>` → `/home/<user>` across `sessions/`, and add the same redaction pass to `gen_sessions.py` so regenerations stay clean.
3. **Gitignore** — add `sessions/` to `.gitignore` so it can't be committed accidentally.

Want me to do 2, 3, or both?

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  05:22:06; model 1m28s

> 💭 (thinking)

The match is `<redacted-name>` at line 3904 — and it reveals a subtler problem: it's the **redaction rule's own source** (`re.compile(r"\b<redacted-name>\b")`) embedded in this session's transcript, and my `\b` anchor can't match its own backslash-escaped form. Worse: hardcoding the name/email in the script means **`sessions/gen_sessions.py` itself leaks the PII**.

The right fix is to **detect** the values to redact at runtime (from `git config` + the environment) so nothing sensitive is hardcoded, and match them as literal substrings. Let me rework that.

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  05:23:06; model 12.6s

All three changes are done and verified.

## What changed in `gen_sessions.py`

**1. Filename format → `yyyy-mm-dd_hh-mm_hex.md`**
Derived from each session's start time (`file_stamp()`), with a 12-hex-char id suffix that disambiguates the three Codex sessions sharing the `019e8b7f` prefix. Files now sort chronologically by name, e.g. `claude/2026-06-03_02-40_22c92cdfa670.md`.

**2. Redaction of email, name, username**
Applied to every byte written under `sessions/` (transcripts + README + the redacted `Source:` path in each header). Markers in the output: 298× `/home/<user>`, 27× `<redacted-name>`, 15× `<redacted-email>`. Residue scan = **zero**.

**3. Targets discovered at runtime, not hardcoded** — the important subtlety
The first attempt hardcoded `<redacted-name>` / the email / `/home/<user>` in the `REDACTIONS` list, which meant the script copied into `sessions/` *itself* leaked the PII, and the `\b`-anchored name pattern couldn't even match its own backslash-escaped form embedded in this conversation's transcript (the lone residue at line 3904). Now `build_redactions()` pulls the values from `git config user.name/user.email` + `getpass.getuser()`/`$HOME` at run time and matches them as **literal substrings**, so:
- nothing sensitive is hardcoded — `grep` confirms the published `sessions/gen_sessions.py` is clean;
- even values embedded in quoted source/JSON inside a transcript get caught.

## Verification
- 14/14 README file links resolve, 0 broken.
- No `m1el…@…`, `<redacted-name>`, or `/home/<user>` anywhere in `sessions/` (including the cached `openrouter_models.json`).
- `Source:` paths now read `/home/<user>/…`.

Costs are unchanged in method (gpt-5.5 still reconciles to $4.10; Codex cached-token caveat still noted); totals drift by a few thousand tokens each run only because session `86d5d0a1` is this live conversation. The files are still **untracked** — say the word if you want `sessions/` gitignored or committed.

Fixed. Tool results are no longer attributed to the human.

**What changed in `parse_claude`:** a `user`-role message is now split — genuine human text renders under `### 👤 User`, while `tool_result` blocks render under their own `### 🛠️ Tool result(s)` header. Only real human messages count toward the turn tally.

**Verification:**
- Turn counts are now meaningful — e.g. session 2 went from `391 user / 374 assistant` to **`12 human / 374 assistant`** (the 379 tool outputs are no longer counted as human turns).
- Mislabel check: **0** `User` headers followed by tool-result content.
- Tool results now appear as `### 🛠️ Tool result` sections in the flow (assistant tool call → tool result → assistant), and I also tag `is_error` results with `(error)`.

The only `↩︎ tool result` strings left anywhere are 2 in this live session's own transcript — they're the literal `old_string`/`new_string` of *this very edit* (me replacing that old label), captured as meta-content, not actual mislabeled output.

### 🤖 **Assistant**  ·  05:35:42; model 26.9s

> 💭 (thinking)
> 

Yes — there's good timing data, and "how the time is spent" is very computable. Here's what's available and a real breakdown from one session (the 558-turn `5ac1a84a`):

**What exists**
- **Claude**: every line has a millisecond `timestamp`. Tool durations are exact — each `tool_use` has an `id`, each `tool_result` a matching `tool_use_id`, so I can difference them. There's also a `durationMs` on a `system` line, but it's *not* whole-session (8.1 min vs 303 min wall) — ignore it; the per-event timestamps are the real source.
- **Codex**: `function_call` → `function_call_output` timestamps give tool durations too, but events are flushed in batches (several share an identical timestamp), so Codex timing is coarser/less trustworthy than Claude's.

**Sample breakdown** (`5ac1a84a`):
- Wall-clock first→last event: **303 min** — but most is human idle (session spanned hours with breaks).
- Tool execution: **12.7 min** across 559 calls.
- By tool: `Bash` 749s (267 calls, avg 2.8s, **max 120s** — a long Coq build/proof check) dominates; `Edit` 7.6s/145, `Read` 2.7s/112, everything else negligible.

So the picture is: tool time is almost entirely `Bash` (builds/checks), edits and reads are instant, and the rest of wall-clock is model generation + you being away.

**The one design choice** before I wire it in: wall-clock is misleading because of idle gaps. I'd split each session into **tool time** (exact), **model time** (gaps from tool-result/user → the assistant's response), and **idle** (gaps over a threshold, default ~120s, = away-from-keyboard), so "active time" is meaningful.

Want me to add a **Timing** section to each per-session file (active time, tool-vs-model split, slowest tools + slowest single calls) and an aggregate to the README? I'll use the 120s idle cap unless you'd prefer a different threshold.

### 👤 **User**  ·  05:39:24; waited 3m33s

if the gaps are "waiting for user", that can be classified that way. so the session would be [waiting for user][model][tool][model][waiting for user], which is perfectly fine. would be nice to have timing information associated with each section in the output. e.g. "👤 User \n <timestamp>; 20s" "🔧 tool → Bash \n <timestamp>; 4s"

### 👤 **User**  ·  05:39:42; waited 18.4s

if the gaps are "waiting for user", that can be classified that way. so the session would be [waiting for user][model][tool][model][waiting for user], which is perfectly fine. would be nice to have timing information associated with each section in the output. e.g. "👤 User \n <timestamp>; 20s" "🔧 tool → Bash \n <timestamp>; 4s", plus a summary of where the time was spent

63	                continue

65	def trunc(s, n=TOOL_TRUNC):
66	    s = s if isinstance(s, str) else json.dumps(s, ensure_ascii=False)
67	    if len(s) > n:
68	        return s[:n] + f"\n… [truncated {len(s)-n} chars]"
69	    return s
70	
71	def fmt_ts(ts):
72	    if not ts:
73	        return "?"
74	    try:
75	        return datetime.fromisoformat(ts.replace("Z", "+00:00")).strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%SZ")
76	    except Exception:
77	        return ts
78	
79	def first_prompt(text_blocks):
80	    """First human prompt that isn't a tag wrapper / caveat / system reminder."""
81	    for t in text_blocks:
82	        s = t.strip()
83	        if not s:
84	            continue
85	        # skip XML-ish wrappers (system-reminder, command-*, local-command-caveat,
86	        # environment_context, …) and command caveats / interrupt markers
87	        if s[0] == "<" or s.startswith("Caveat:") or s.startswith("[Request interrupted"):
88	            continue
89	        return s
90	    return text_blocks[0].strip() if text_blocks else ""
91

93	def parse_claude(path):
94	    sid = os.path.basename(path).replace(".jsonl", "")

152	def parse_claude(path):
153	    sid = os.path.basename(path).replace(".jsonl", "")
154	    models, n_user, n_tool = set(), 0, 0
155	    tok = dict(input=0, output=0, cache_create=0, cache_read=0)
156	    usage_by_req = {}          # requestId -> usage (dedupe split-block lines)
157	    first_ts = last_ts = None
158	    user_prompts, last_assistant_text = [], ""
159	    lines = []
160	    cur_rid, cur_body = None, []   # group consecutive same-requestId assistant blocks into one turn
161	
162	    def flush_turn():
163	        if cur_body:
164	            lines.append("### 🤖 **Assistant**\n\n" + "\n\n".join(cur_body) + "\n")
165	
166	    for d in jlines(path):
167	        typ = d.get("type")
168	        ts = d.get("timestamp")
169	        if ts:
170	            first_ts = first_ts or ts
171	            last_ts = ts
172	        if typ not in ("user", "assistant"):
173	            continue
174	        msg = d.get("message", {}) or {}
175	        role = msg.get("role", typ)
176	        content = msg.get("content")
177	        blocks = content if isinstance(content, list) else [{"type": "text", "text": content}]
178	        text_blocks, rendered, tool_results = [], [], []
179	        for b in blocks:
180	            if not isinstance(b, dict):
181	                rendered.append(str(b)); continue
182	            bt = b.get("type")
183	            if bt == "text":

196	                tool_results.append(f"```\n{trunc(c)}\n```{tag}")

199	                models.add(msg["model"])
200	            rid = d.get("requestId") or d.get("uuid")
201	            u = msg.get("usage")
202	            if u and rid not in usage_by_req:     # count usage once per API request
203	                usage_by_req[rid] = u
204	            jointext = "\n".join(text_blocks).strip()
205	            if jointext:
206	                last_assistant_text = jointext
207	            if rid != cur_rid:                     # new turn -> flush previous

209	            cur_body.extend(r for r in rendered if r.strip())
210	        else:
211	            # A "user"-role message is either a real human turn or just the
212	            # tool_result(s) returned for the assistant's last tool calls. Only
213	            # the former is a human turn; render results under their own header.
214	            flush_turn(); cur_rid, cur_body = None, []

Done. The transcripts are now timeline-aware, exactly as you described.

## What each transcript now shows

Every section carries a timestamp and its phase duration, and the session reads as `[waiting for user][model][tool][model]…`:
```
### 👤 User  ·  11:21:59
### 🤖 Assistant  ·  11:22:02; model 4.1s
**🔧 tool → Bash**  ·  157ms
### 🛠️ Tool result  ·  11:22:04; tool 157ms
```
Per-call exec times are **matched exactly** (`tool_use` ↔ `tool_result` by id, `function_call` ↔ `output` by call_id) and printed inline on each call line.

## Summaries

Each file gets a **## Timing** block (wall-clock · active · waiting; model vs tool; tool time by name; slowest calls), e.g. for the big session:
- wall **5h03m** · active **3h24m** · waiting 1h39m; tool exec 12m40s with `Bash` 12m29s/267 calls dominating.

And the README has an **aggregate time** table:

| Agent | Wall | Model | Tool | Active | Waiting |
|---|--:|--:|--:|--:|--:|
| Claude Code | 21h18m | 11h05m | 41m05s | 11h46m | 9h32m |
| Codex | 29m36s | 17m05s | 1m13s | 18m18s | 11m17s |

## How time is attributed
Each section's interval `[prev.end, this.end]` is assigned by what the section *is* — `👤 User`→waiting-for-user, `🤖 Assistant`→model, `🛠️ Tool result`→tool — so the three buckets **tile the session and sum to wall-clock** (no idle threshold needed; long pre-message gaps are just "waiting", as you wanted). Per-session tables gained `Active`/`Wall` columns.

Caveats kept honest: Claude timestamps are per-block and precise; Codex events are batch-flushed, so its splits are flagged *approximate* in every Codex file and in the README note. Redaction still holds (0 residue), 14/14 links resolve, and `sessions/gen_sessions.py` is updated.

One imperfection worth flagging: the "model" bucket absorbs any non-tool, non-waiting gap — including background `ScheduleWakeup` sleeps between two assistant turns — so a session that idled on a scheduled wake will show inflated "model" time. The inline per-section durations make that visible (you'd see one section with an outsized `model …`), but if you'd rather I split those out as a separate "idle/scheduled" phase, I can.

### 🛠️ **Tool result**  ·  06:12:18; tool 31ms

```
94	    s = float(s)
95	    if s < 1:
96	        return f"{s*1000:.0f}ms"
97	    if s < 60:
98	        return f"{s:.1f}s"
99	    m, sec = divmod(int(round(s)), 60)
100	    if m < 60:
101	        return f"{m}m{sec:02d}s"
102	    h, m = divmod(m, 60)
103	    return f"{h}h{m:02d}m"
104	
105	def render_sections(sections):
106	    """Turn timed sections into transcript markdown + a timing breakdown.
107	
108	    Each section's interval [prev.end, this.end] is attributed to one phase by the
109	    section's kind: user→waiting-for-user, assistant→model, toolresult→tool. The
110	    intervals tile the whole session, so the buckets sum to wall-clock. Per-tool
111	    exec times (matched call→result) are rendered inline on the call lines."""
112	    out, timing = [], dict(waiting=0.0, model=0.0, tool=0.0, wall=0.0)
113	    prev_end = None
114	    for s in sections:
115	        ts = s.get("ts")
116	        end = s.get("end") if s.get("end") is not None else ts
117	        dur = (end - prev_end) if (prev_end is not None and end is not None) else None
118	        if dur is not None and dur >= 0:
119	            timing[{"user": "waiting", "assistant": "model", "toolresult": "tool"}[s["kind"]]] += dur
120	        if s["kind"] == "user":
121	            head, phase = "### 👤 **User**", "waited"
122	        elif s["kind"] == "assistant":
123	            head, phase = "### 🤖 **Assistant**", "model"
124	        else:
125	            head, phase = f"### 🛠️ **{s.get('hdr','Tool result')}**", "tool"
126	        meta = clock(s.get("ts_str", ""))
127	        if dur is not None and dur > 0:
128	            meta += f"; {phase} {fmt_dur(dur)}"
129	        out.append(f"{head}  ·  {meta}\n\n{s['body']}\n")
130	        if end is not None:
131	            prev_end = end
132	    if sections:
133	        f0 = sections[0].get("ts"); ln = sections[-1].get("end") or sections[-1].get("ts")
134	        if f0 is not None and ln is not None:
135	            timing["wall"] = ln - f0
```
